Acceptance and Rejection of Bequests
Rulings on acceptance and absence in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on acceptance and rejection of bequests, distinguishing between cases of absence and presence at the testator's death.

Core Idea
A bequest requires acceptance; absence at death is treated as rejection but later acceptance restores the bequest.

This lesson examines a narration from Abu Yusuf on how acceptance and rejection of a bequest are determined, particularly when the legatee is absent at the testator's death. Understanding these rules is vital for correctly implementing last wishes in estate law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and rulings
Locate two scenarios: a conditional bequest requiring Hajj and a bequest of ongoing support to an absent legatee. Each has a distinct ruling based on acceptance.
The Hajj condition does not invalidate the bequest; acceptance remains key.
2
Analyze the absent legatee ruling
If the legatee is absent at death, it is like rejection and he gets nothing. But if he later comes and accepts, he gets what has passed (retroactive effect).
The same applies if he appears and does not accept.
3
Extract the underlying principle
The bequest is not automatically binding; it requires the legatee's active acceptance after the testator's death. Absence alone is not final rejection.
This differs from gifts inter vivos where acceptance may be immediate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي نوادر بشر عن أبي يوسف في الإملاء : إذا أوصى بثلثه لرجل على أن يحج عنه فهذا جائز إن قبل ذلك الموصى له ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف : إذا قال في وصيته ينفق على فلان كذا والموصى له غائب أو مات الموصي وهو غائب فهو بمنزلة رد الوصية ولا شيء له، وكذلك إن قدم فلم يقبل، وإن قدم وقبل فله ما مضى. قال أبو يوسف : أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وقال أن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له الأول أو لم يأب فالثلث للأول ولو أبي كان للآخر، لو قال ثلثي وصية لفلان فإن لم يشأ ذلك فلفلان فهو مثل الأول، ولو قال ثلثي وصية لفلان إن شاء وإن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له قبل أن يتكلم بشيء فالثلث مردود على الورثة. ابن سماعة عن محمد: رجل أوصى لرجل بوصية ولا لفلان فقال فلان لا هي وقال إن لم يقبل فلان ما أوصيت له به أو قال إن رد فلان ما أوصيت به فهو لفلان فإذا الموصى له الأول حياً أو كان حياً فمات قبل الموصي ولم يعلم بالوصية قال هي للثاني كلها إن أسلمت جاريتي هذه فأعتقوها فباعوها قبل أن تسلم ثم أسلمت بعد مضي البيع صح ترد. قال أبو حنيفة : إذا قال أوصيت أن يخدم عبدي فلاناً سنة ثم هو أقبل الوصية قال : يخدم الورثة سنة ثم الموصى له ولا تبطل وصيته للثاني بأباء الأول الخدمة. قال أعطوه فلاناً بعد السنة فإن مات فلان خدم تمام السنة للورثة ثم يدفع إلى الموصى له بعد تمام السنة. وقال أبو حنيفة هذه وصية فيها يمين وليست المسألة الأولى كهذه ابراهيم بن رستم عن محمد قال أرضي التي في موضع كذا وغلامي فلان لأم ولده فيصير ميراثاً منها . ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف : أوصى أن ينفق على أم ولده ما قامت على ولدها وقال إن تزوجت فلا شيء لها فتزوجت وطلقها زوجها فرجعت إلى ولدها لم يرد عليها ما كان أوصى به لها وقد بطل ذلك، وكذلك إن خرجت من بلادها إلى بلاد أخرى، ولو خرجت من دارها أو جاء منها شيء يعرف أنها قد تركتهم ولم تقم عليهم فلا هذه الدار لك على أن تحج في سبيل الله أو قال هذه الدابة لك على أن تغزوا عليها في سبيل الله قال : له وله أن يصنع بها ما شاء. عن أبي يوسف : رجل أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وشرط عليه أن يقضي دينه معناه شرط الموصي على الموصى له أن يقضي دين الموصي فهذا على وجوه : إن كان الدين مجهولاً أو كان معلوماً إلا أن الثلث مجهول فالوصية باطلة وإن كان الدين معلوماً والثلث معلوماً فإن لم يكن في الثلث ذهب ولا فضة فهو جائز ويجب له الثلث بالدين إذا قبل كما يجب في البيع، وإن كان في الثلث دراهم إن كان أكثر من الدين فإن هذا لا يجوز من قبيل أن هذا دراهم بدراهم وفضل عروض سوى ذلك، وإن كانت الدراهم التي في الثلث أقل من الدين جاز، فإن قبض الثلث ساعة يموت أو قبض الدراهم التي في الثلث ساعة يموت وقضى الدين ساعته انتقص ذلك في الدراهم ما يخصه وجاز في العروض. أوصى بألف درهم على أن يقضي عنه فلاناً خمسمائة لا يجوز ولو قال على أن يقضي فلاناً منها خمسمائة جاز العلاء في نوادر هشام عن أبي يوسف : إذا قال إذا مت وهذان العبدان في ملكي فهما وصية لفلان فمات أحد العبدين ثم مات الموصي والثاني في ملكه فالوصية باطلة ولو قال إن مت وفلان وفلان حيان فهذا العبد وصية لهما فمات أحدهما قبل موت الموصي فإن الثاني منهما يعطي نصف العبد . قال : وإذا أوصى رجل لأمته أن تعتق على أن تتزوج ثم مات الموصي الأمة لا أتزوج فإنها تعتق ويجب أن يعلم بأن الموصي متى علق عتق مملوكه بشيء بعد موته فإنه لا يخلو من وجهين : أن يعلقه على فعل غير مؤقت بأن قال هي حرة إن ثبتت على الإسلام بعد موتي أو أوصى أن يعتقوها بعد موته على أن لا تتزوج أو قال هي حرة بعد موتي إن لم تتزوج أو علق عتقه على فعل مؤقت بأن قال إن مكثت مع ولدي شهراً فهي حرة أو بيع فقالت
And in the Nawadir of Bishr from Abu Yusuf in al-Imla': If he bequeaths one-third to a man on condition that he perform Hajj on his behalf, it is permissible if the legatee accepts. Ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf: If he says in his bequest 'spend such-and-such on so-and-so' and the legatee is absent, or the testator dies while he is absent, it is equivalent to rejection of the bequest and he gets nothing. Similarly if he comes and does not accept. But if he comes and accepts, he gets what has passed. Abu Yusuf said: He bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and says 'if he refuses, it is for so-and-so.' Then the first legatee dies or does not refuse: one-third is for the first; if he refuses, it is for the other. If he says 'one-third is a bequest for so-and-so; if he does not wish it, then for so-and-so,' it is like the first. If he says 'one-third is a bequest for so-and-so; if he wishes, and if he refuses, then for so-and-so,' and the legatee dies before saying anything, the one-third reverts to the heirs. Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad: A man bequeaths a bequest to a man and to so-and-so, and so-and-so says 'no, it is [for the other]'. And if he says 'if so-and-so does not accept my bequest to him' or 'if so-and-so rejects my bequest, then it is for so-and-so,' then if the first legatee is alive or was alive and died before the testator unaware of the bequest, he said: it is all for the second. 'If my slave-girl becomes Muslim, free her.' They sold her before she became Muslim, then she became Muslim after the sale had passed; the sale is valid (tard?). Abu Hanifa said: If he says 'I bequeath that my slave serve so-and-so for a year, then he is free,' and the legatee accepts the bequest, he said: the slave serves the heirs for a year, then the legatee, and his bequest to the second is not invalidated by the first's refusal of service. He said: Give him to so-and-so after the year. If so-and-so dies, the slave completes the year for the heirs, then is given to the legatee after the year. And Abu Hanifa said: This bequest contains an oath; the first issue is not like this. Ibrahim ibn Rustam from Muhammad said: 'My land in such place and my slave so-and-so are for my umm walad' – it becomes inheritance from her. Ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf: He bequeaths that maintenance be given to his umm walad as long as she cares for his children, and says 'if she marries, nothing for her.' She marries, but her husband divorces her and she returns to his children: he never returns to her what was bequeathed; it is cancelled. Similarly if she leaves her country to another country. Even if she leaves her house, or something comes from her indicating she has abandoned them and does not care for them, [it is cancelled]. 'This house is for you on condition that you perform Hajj in the way of Allah,' or he said 'this animal is for you on condition that you perform ghazw with it in the way of Allah,' he said: it is for him, and he may do with it as he wishes. From Abu Yusuf: A man bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and stipulates that he pay his debt. The meaning is that the testator stipulates on the legatee to pay the testator's debt. This has aspects: If the debt is unknown, or known but the one-third is unknown, the bequest is void. If the debt is known and the one-third is known, and the one-third contains no gold or silver, it is permissible, and he is obligated to [pay] the one-third for the debt if he accepts, as in a sale. If there are dirhams in the one-third and it is more than the debt, it is not permissible because it is dirhams for dirhams with an excess of goods besides. If the dirhams in the one-third are less than the debt, it is permissible. If he takes possession of the one-third at the hour of death, or takes the dirhams in the one-third at the hour of death and pays the debt immediately, he deducts from the dirhams what is appropriate, and it is permissible for the goods. He bequeaths a thousand dirhams on condition that he pay someone five hundred on his behalf: not permissible. If he says 'on condition that he pay so-and-so five hundred from them,' it is permissible. Al-‘Ala in the Nawadir of Hisham from Abu Yusuf: If he says 'when I die and these two slaves are in my possession, they are a bequest for so-and-so' and one slave dies, then the testator dies and the second is in his possession: the bequest is void. If he says 'when I die and so-and-so and so-and-so are alive, this slave is a bequest for them' and one of them dies before the testator's death: the other of them takes half the slave. He said: If a man bequeaths that his female slave be freed on condition that she marry, then the testator dies, and the slave girl says 'I will not marry,' she is freed. And it must be known that when the testator attaches the freeing of his slave to something after his death, it is either of two ways: He attaches it to a non-time-bound action, like 'she is free if she remains Muslim after my death' or 'he bequeaths that they free her after his death on condition that she does not marry' or 'she is free after my death if she does not marry.' Or he attaches her freeing to a time-bound action, like 'if she stays with my child for a month, she is free' or 'if she is sold and she says [incomplete]'
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles numerous transmitted rulings (nawadir) on conditional bequests, acceptance, rejection, and related issues. Key points include: (1) A bequest conditioned on performing Hajj is valid if accepted. (2) If a legatee is absent at the testator's death, it is treated as rejection unless he later accepts and gets the past benefit. (3) Scenarios where a bequest is made to an alternative if the first refuses; rulings depend on whether the first dies before or after the testator, and whether he had knowledge. (4) Bequests of service followed by freedom: the slave serves the heirs first if the legatee refuses? (5) Bequest to a wife/mother (umm walad) conditioned on caring for children; if she marries or leaves, it is cancelled. (6) Bequest conditioned on performing Hajj or jihad: the recipient owns the property and may use it freely. (7) Bequest with condition to pay a debt: validity depends on whether debt and one-third are known, and whether the one-third contains cash; if dirhams exceed debt, it is invalid due to riba. (8) Bequest of slaves conditional on survival: if one slave dies before testator, the bequest fails. (9) Bequest to free a slave conditioned on marriage: if the slave refuses marriage, she is freed. The passage ends with a classification of conditional freeing (ta'liq al-‘itq) after death: non-time-bound vs. time-bound.

Key Terms
نوادر (nawadir): Rare or isolated narrations within the Hanafi school, not from the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will; a disposition of property to take effect after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration, what happens if a legatee is absent at the testator's death and does not accept afterwards?
A) The bequest goes to the heirs automatically
B) The bequest is held for the legatee indefinitely
C) The bequest is considered rejected and the legatee gets nothing
D) The bequest is transferred to the legatee's estate

Key Takeaway
A bequest requires the legatee's acceptance; absence at death does not automatically void it if acceptance comes later.

Alternative Bequests: When the First Legatee Refuses or Dies
Rulings on alternative bequests with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the entitlement of a secondary legatee in alternative bequests based on the death or refusal of the primary legatee.

Core Idea
In alternative bequests, the second legatee inherits only if the first legatee refuses or dies without acceptance.

This lesson covers cases where a testator designates an alternative legatee if the first refuses or does not wish the bequest. The rulings from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad clarify how to handle death before acceptance, and the difference between conditional phrasing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the alternative bequest scenarios
Three wordings are presented: (1) 'if he refuses, it is for X', (2) 'if he does not wish it, then for X', (3) 'if he wishes, and if he refuses, then for X'.
Each has different implications for when the first legatee dies before acting.
2
Analyze the effect of the first legatee's death
In first two wordings, if the first dies or accepts, the bequest stays with him; only if he refuses does it pass. In the third, if he dies before speaking, the bequest returns to the heirs.
The third wording effectively makes the bequest conditional on the first legatee's explicit acceptance during life.
3
Extract the principle
Alternative bequests are valid; the testator's phrasing determines whether the second legatee takes only upon refusal or also upon death without acceptance.
The key is whether the condition is attached to the act of refusal or to the death itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي نوادر بشر عن أبي يوسف في الإملاء : إذا أوصى بثلثه لرجل على أن يحج عنه فهذا جائز إن قبل ذلك الموصى له ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف : إذا قال في وصيته ينفق على فلان كذا والموصى له غائب أو مات الموصي وهو غائب فهو بمنزلة رد الوصية ولا شيء له، وكذلك إن قدم فلم يقبل، وإن قدم وقبل فله ما مضى. قال أبو يوسف : أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وقال أن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له الأول أو لم يأب فالثلث للأول ولو أبي كان للآخر، لو قال ثلثي وصية لفلان فإن لم يشأ ذلك فلفلان فهو مثل الأول، ولو قال ثلثي وصية لفلان إن شاء وإن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له قبل أن يتكلم بشيء فالثلث مردود على الورثة. ابن سماعة عن محمد: رجل أوصى لرجل بوصية ولا لفلان فقال فلان لا هي وقال إن لم يقبل فلان ما أوصيت له به أو قال إن رد فلان ما أوصيت به فهو لفلان فإذا الموصى له الأول حياً أو كان حياً فمات قبل الموصي ولم يعلم بالوصية قال هي للثاني كلها إن أسلمت جاريتي هذه فأعتقوها فباعوها قبل أن تسلم ثم أسلمت بعد مضي البيع صح ترد. قال أبو حنيفة : إذا قال أوصيت أن يخدم عبدي فلاناً سنة ثم هو أقبل الوصية قال : يخدم الورثة سنة ثم الموصى له ولا تبطل وصيته للثاني بأباء الأول الخدمة. قال أعطوه فلاناً بعد السنة فإن مات فلان خدم تمام السنة للورثة ثم يدفع إلى الموصى له بعد تمام السنة. وقال أبو حنيفة هذه وصية فيها يمين وليست المسألة الأولى كهذه ابراهيم بن رستم عن محمد قال أرضي التي في موضع كذا وغلامي فلان لأم ولده فيصير ميراثاً منها . ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف : أوصى أن ينفق على أم ولده ما قامت على ولدها وقال إن تزوجت فلا شيء لها فتزوجت وطلقها زوجها فرجعت إلى ولدها لم يرد عليها ما كان أوصى به لها وقد بطل ذلك، وكذلك إن خرجت من بلادها إلى بلاد أخرى، ولو خرجت من دارها أو جاء منها شيء يعرف أنها قد تركتهم ولم تقم عليهم فلا هذه الدار لك على أن تحج في سبيل الله أو قال هذه الدابة لك على أن تغزوا عليها في سبيل الله قال : له وله أن يصنع بها ما شاء. عن أبي يوسف : رجل أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وشرط عليه أن يقضي دينه معناه شرط الموصي على الموصى له أن يقضي دين الموصي فهذا على وجوه : إن كان الدين مجهولاً أو كان معلوماً إلا أن الثلث مجهول فالوصية باطلة وإن كان الدين معلوماً والثلث معلوماً فإن لم يكن في الثلث ذهب ولا فضة فهو جائز ويجب له الثلث بالدين إذا قبل كما يجب في البيع، وإن كان في الثلث دراهم إن كان أكثر من الدين فإن هذا لا يجوز من قبيل أن هذا دراهم بدراهم وفضل عروض سوى ذلك، وإن كانت الدراهم التي في الثلث أقل من الدين جاز، فإن قبض الثلث ساعة يموت أو قبض الدراهم التي في الثلث ساعة يموت وقضى الدين ساعته انتقص ذلك في الدراهم ما يخصه وجاز في العروض. أوصى بألف درهم على أن يقضي عنه فلاناً خمسمائة لا يجوز ولو قال على أن يقضي فلاناً منها خمسمائة جاز العلاء في نوادر هشام عن أبي يوسف : إذا قال إذا مت وهذان العبدان في ملكي فهما وصية لفلان فمات أحد العبدين ثم مات الموصي والثاني في ملكه فالوصية باطلة ولو قال إن مت وفلان وفلان حيان فهذا العبد وصية لهما فمات أحدهما قبل موت الموصي فإن الثاني منهما يعطي نصف العبد . قال : وإذا أوصى رجل لأمته أن تعتق على أن تتزوج ثم مات الموصي الأمة لا أتزوج فإنها تعتق ويجب أن يعلم بأن الموصي متى علق عتق مملوكه بشيء بعد موته فإنه لا يخلو من وجهين : أن يعلقه على فعل غير مؤقت بأن قال هي حرة إن ثبتت على الإسلام بعد موتي أو أوصى أن يعتقوها بعد موته على أن لا تتزوج أو قال هي حرة بعد موتي إن لم تتزوج أو علق عتقه على فعل مؤقت بأن قال إن مكثت مع ولدي شهراً فهي حرة أو بيع فقالت
And in the Nawadir of Bishr from Abu Yusuf in al-Imla': If he bequeaths one-third to a man on condition that he perform Hajj on his behalf, it is permissible if the legatee accepts. Ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf: If he says in his bequest 'spend such-and-such on so-and-so' and the legatee is absent, or the testator dies while he is absent, it is equivalent to rejection of the bequest and he gets nothing. Similarly if he comes and does not accept. But if he comes and accepts, he gets what has passed. Abu Yusuf said: He bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and says 'if he refuses, it is for so-and-so.' Then the first legatee dies or does not refuse: one-third is for the first; if he refuses, it is for the other. If he says 'one-third is a bequest for so-and-so; if he does not wish it, then for so-and-so,' it is like the first. If he says 'one-third is a bequest for so-and-so; if he wishes, and if he refuses, then for so-and-so,' and the legatee dies before saying anything, the one-third reverts to the heirs. Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad: A man bequeaths a bequest to a man and to so-and-so, and so-and-so says 'no, it is [for the other]'. And if he says 'if so-and-so does not accept my bequest to him' or 'if so-and-so rejects my bequest, then it is for so-and-so,' then if the first legatee is alive or was alive and died before the testator unaware of the bequest, he said: it is all for the second. 'If my slave-girl becomes Muslim, free her.' They sold her before she became Muslim, then she became Muslim after the sale had passed; the sale is valid (tard?). Abu Hanifa said: If he says 'I bequeath that my slave serve so-and-so for a year, then he is free,' and the legatee accepts the bequest, he said: the slave serves the heirs for a year, then the legatee, and his bequest to the second is not invalidated by the first's refusal of service. He said: Give him to so-and-so after the year. If so-and-so dies, the slave completes the year for the heirs, then is given to the legatee after the year. And Abu Hanifa said: This bequest contains an oath; the first issue is not like this. Ibrahim ibn Rustam from Muhammad said: 'My land in such place and my slave so-and-so are for my umm walad' – it becomes inheritance from her. Ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf: He bequeaths that maintenance be given to his umm walad as long as she cares for his children, and says 'if she marries, nothing for her.' She marries, but her husband divorces her and she returns to his children: he never returns to her what was bequeathed; it is cancelled. Similarly if she leaves her country to another country. Even if she leaves her house, or something comes from her indicating she has abandoned them and does not care for them, [it is cancelled]. 'This house is for you on condition that you perform Hajj in the way of Allah,' or he said 'this animal is for you on condition that you perform ghazw with it in the way of Allah,' he said: it is for him, and he may do with it as he wishes. From Abu Yusuf: A man bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and stipulates that he pay his debt. The meaning is that the testator stipulates on the legatee to pay the testator's debt. This has aspects: If the debt is unknown, or known but the one-third is unknown, the bequest is void. If the debt is known and the one-third is known, and the one-third contains no gold or silver, it is permissible, and he is obligated to [pay] the one-third for the debt if he accepts, as in a sale. If there are dirhams in the one-third and it is more than the debt, it is not permissible because it is dirhams for dirhams with an excess of goods besides. If the dirhams in the one-third are less than the debt, it is permissible. If he takes possession of the one-third at the hour of death, or takes the dirhams in the one-third at the hour of death and pays the debt immediately, he deducts from the dirhams what is appropriate, and it is permissible for the goods. He bequeaths a thousand dirhams on condition that he pay someone five hundred on his behalf: not permissible. If he says 'on condition that he pay so-and-so five hundred from them,' it is permissible. Al-‘Ala in the Nawadir of Hisham from Abu Yusuf: If he says 'when I die and these two slaves are in my possession, they are a bequest for so-and-so' and one slave dies, then the testator dies and the second is in his possession: the bequest is void. If he says 'when I die and so-and-so and so-and-so are alive, this slave is a bequest for them' and one of them dies before the testator's death: the other of them takes half the slave. He said: If a man bequeaths that his female slave be freed on condition that she marry, then the testator dies, and the slave girl says 'I will not marry,' she is freed. And it must be known that when the testator attaches the freeing of his slave to something after his death, it is either of two ways: He attaches it to a non-time-bound action, like 'she is free if she remains Muslim after my death' or 'he bequeaths that they free her after his death on condition that she does not marry' or 'she is free after my death if she does not marry.' Or he attaches her freeing to a time-bound action, like 'if she stays with my child for a month, she is free' or 'if she is sold and she says [incomplete]'
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles numerous transmitted rulings (nawadir) on conditional bequests, acceptance, rejection, and related issues. Key points include: (1) A bequest conditioned on performing Hajj is valid if accepted. (2) If a legatee is absent at the testator's death, it is treated as rejection unless he later accepts and gets the past benefit. (3) Scenarios where a bequest is made to an alternative if the first refuses; rulings depend on whether the first dies before or after the testator, and whether he had knowledge. (4) Bequests of service followed by freedom: the slave serves the heirs first if the legatee refuses? (5) Bequest to a wife/mother (umm walad) conditioned on caring for children; if she marries or leaves, it is cancelled. (6) Bequest conditioned on performing Hajj or jihad: the recipient owns the property and may use it freely. (7) Bequest with condition to pay a debt: validity depends on whether debt and one-third are known, and whether the one-third contains cash; if dirhams exceed debt, it is invalid due to riba. (8) Bequest of slaves conditional on survival: if one slave dies before testator, the bequest fails. (9) Bequest to free a slave conditioned on marriage: if the slave refuses marriage, she is freed. The passage ends with a classification of conditional freeing (ta'liq al-‘itq) after death: non-time-bound vs. time-bound.

Key Terms
نوادر (nawadir): Rare or isolated narrations within the Hanafi school, not from the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Using the first scenario from Abu Yusuf, if the testator says 'if he refuses, it is for so-and-so' and the first legatee does not refuse but dies after the testator, who gets the bequest?
A) The second legatee
B) The first legatee's heirs
C) The testator's heirs
D) The second legatee and heirs share

Key Takeaway
The testator's precise phrasing determines whether an alternative bequest takes effect upon refusal or only upon explicit rejection.

Bequests with Conditions of Service, Hajj, and Jihad
Rulings on conditions involving worship and service

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions that are enforceable (like service) and those that are not (like Hajj/jihad) in bequests, and state the Hanafi ruling on ownership.

Core Idea
A condition requiring an act of worship (Hajj, jihad) does not restrict ownership; the legatee owns the property freely.

This lesson examines bequests conditioned on performing acts of worship (Hajj) or service. The Hanafi ruling is that once the legatee accepts, the property is owned absolutely, and the condition is merely a recommendation, not a binding restriction. However, a condition of service (e.g., serving for a year) can be valid and enforceable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of conditions
First: condition to perform Hajj or jihad (worship). Second: condition to serve (service contract).
The ruling differs fundamentally.
2
Analyze the Hajj/jihad condition
The text says 'he owns it and may do with it as he wishes' – the condition is not binding; the bequest is absolute.
This is because the condition is not a financial obligation but a religious one.
3
Analyze the service condition (slave serving for a year then free)
Abu Hanifa says this is a valid bequest with an oath; the slave serves the heirs for a year if the legatee refuses service? Actually the text says the slave serves the heirs for a year then goes to the legatee.
The condition of service is enforceable because it is a benefit to the estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

غائب فهو بمنزلة رد الوصية ولا شيء له، وكذلك إن قدم فلم يقبل، وإن قدم وقبل فله ما مضى. قال أبو يوسف : أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وقال أن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له الأول أو لم يأب فالثلث للأول ولو أبي كان أوصى لرجل بوصية ولا لفلان فقال فلان لا هي وقال إن لم يقبل فلان ما أوصيت له به أو قال إن رد فلان ما أوصيت به فهو لفلان فإذا الموصى له الأول حياً أو كان حياً فمات قبل الموصي ولم يعلم بالوصية قال هي للثاني كلها إن أسلمت جاريتي هذه فأعتقوها فباعوها قبل أن تسلم ثم أسلمت بعد مضي البيع صح ترد. قال أبو حنيفة : إذا قال أوصيت أن يخدم عبدي فلاناً سنة ثم هو أقبل الوصية قال : يخدم الورثة سنة ثم الموصى له ولا تبطل وصيته للثاني بأباء الأول الخدمة. قال أعطوه فلاناً بعد السنة فإن مات فلان خدم تمام السنة للورثة ثم يدفع إلى الموصى له بعد تمام السنة. وقال أبو حنيفة هذه وصية فيها يمين وليست المسألة الأولى كهذه ابراهيم بن رستم عن محمد قال أرضي التي في موضع كذا وغلامي فلان لأم ولده فيصير ميراثاً منها . ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف : أوصى أن ينفق على أم ولده ما قامت على ولدها وقال إن تزوجت فلا شيء لها فتزوجت وطلقها زوجها فرجعت إلى ولدها لم يرد عليها ما كان أوصى به لها وقد بطل ذلك، وكذلك إن خرجت من بلادها إلى بلاد أخرى، ولو خرجت من دارها أو جاء منها شيء يعرف أنها قد تركتهم ولم تقم عليهم فلا هذه الدار لك على أن تحج في سبيل الله أو قال هذه الدابة لك على أن تغزوا عليها في سبيل الله قال : له وله أن يصنع بها ما شاء. عن أبي يوسف : رجل أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وشرط عليه أن يقضي دينه معناه شرط الموصي على الموصى له أن يقضي دين الموصي فهذا على وجوه : إن كان الدين مجهولاً أو كان معلوماً إلا أن الثلث مجهول فالوصية باطلة وإن كان الدين معلوماً والثلث معلوماً فإن لم يكن في الثلث ذهب ولا فضة فهو جائز ويجب له الثلث بالدين إذا قبل كما يجب في البيع، وإن كان في الثلث دراهم إن كان أكثر من الدين فإن هذا لا يجوز من قبيل أن هذا دراهم بدراهم وفضل عروض سوى ذلك، وإن كانت الدراهم التي في الثلث أقل من الدين جاز، فإن قبض الثلث ساعة يموت أو قبض الدراهم التي في الثلث ساعة يموت وقضى الدين ساعته انتقص ذلك في الدراهم ما يخصه وجاز في العروض. أوصى بألف درهم على أن يقضي عنه فلاناً خمسمائة لا يجوز ولو قال على أن يقضي فلاناً منها خمسمائة جاز العلاء في نوادر هشام عن أبي يوسف : إذا قال إذا مت وهذان العبدان في ملكي فهما وصية لفلان فمات أحد العبدين ثم مات الموصي والثاني في ملكه فالوصية باطلة ولو قال إن مت وفلان وفلان حيان فهذا العبد وصية لهما فمات أحدهما قبل موت الموصي فإن الثاني منهما يعطي نصف العبد . قال : وإذا أوصى رجل لأمته أن تعتق على أن تتزوج ثم مات الموصي الأمة لا أتزوج فإنها تعتق ويجب أن يعلم بأن الموصي متى علق عتق مملوكه بشيء بعد موته فإنه لا يخلو من وجهين : أن يعلقه على فعل غير مؤقت بأن قال هي حرة إن ثبتت على الإسلام بعد موتي أو أوصى أن يعتقوها بعد موته على أن لا تتزوج أو قال هي حرة بعد موتي إن لم تتزوج أو علق عتقه على فعل مؤقت بأن قال إن مكثت مع ولدي شهراً فهي حرة أو بيع فقالت
And in the Nawadir of Bishr from Abu Yusuf in al-Imla': If he bequeaths one-third to a man on condition that he perform Hajj on his behalf, it is permissible if the legatee accepts. Ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf: If he says in his bequest 'spend such-and-such on so-and-so' and the legatee is absent, or the testator dies while he is absent, it is equivalent to rejection of the bequest and he gets nothing. Similarly if he comes and does not accept. But if he comes and accepts, he gets what has passed. Abu Yusuf said: He bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and says 'if he refuses, it is for so-and-so.' Then the first legatee dies or does not refuse: one-third is for the first; if he refuses, it is for the other. If he says 'one-third is a bequest for so-and-so; if he does not wish it, then for so-and-so,' it is like the first. If he says 'one-third is a bequest for so-and-so; if he wishes, and if he refuses, then for so-and-so,' and the legatee dies before saying anything, the one-third reverts to the heirs. Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad: A man bequeaths a bequest to a man and to so-and-so, and so-and-so says 'no, it is [for the other]'. And if he says 'if so-and-so does not accept my bequest to him' or 'if so-and-so rejects my bequest, then it is for so-and-so,' then if the first legatee is alive or was alive and died before the testator unaware of the bequest, he said: it is all for the second. 'If my slave-girl becomes Muslim, free her.' They sold her before she became Muslim, then she became Muslim after the sale had passed; the sale is valid (tard?). Abu Hanifa said: If he says 'I bequeath that my slave serve so-and-so for a year, then he is free,' and the legatee accepts the bequest, he said: the slave serves the heirs for a year, then the legatee, and his bequest to the second is not invalidated by the first's refusal of service. He said: Give him to so-and-so after the year. If so-and-so dies, the slave completes the year for the heirs, then is given to the legatee after the year. And Abu Hanifa said: This bequest contains an oath; the first issue is not like this. Ibrahim ibn Rustam from Muhammad said: 'My land in such place and my slave so-and-so are for my umm walad' – it becomes inheritance from her. Ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf: He bequeaths that maintenance be given to his umm walad as long as she cares for his children, and says 'if she marries, nothing for her.' She marries, but her husband divorces her and she returns to his children: he never returns to her what was bequeathed; it is cancelled. Similarly if she leaves her country to another country. Even if she leaves her house, or something comes from her indicating she has abandoned them and does not care for them, [it is cancelled]. 'This house is for you on condition that you perform Hajj in the way of Allah,' or he said 'this animal is for you on condition that you perform ghazw with it in the way of Allah,' he said: it is for him, and he may do with it as he wishes. From Abu Yusuf: A man bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and stipulates that he pay his debt. The meaning is that the testator stipulates on the legatee to pay the testator's debt. This has aspects: If the debt is unknown, or known but the one-third is unknown, the bequest is void. If the debt is known and the one-third is known, and the one-third contains no gold or silver, it is permissible, and he is obligated to [pay] the one-third for the debt if he accepts, as in a sale. If there are dirhams in the one-third and it is more than the debt, it is not permissible because it is dirhams for dirhams with an excess of goods besides. If the dirhams in the one-third are less than the debt, it is permissible. If he takes possession of the one-third at the hour of death, or takes the dirhams in the one-third at the hour of death and pays the debt immediately, he deducts from the dirhams what is appropriate, and it is permissible for the goods. He bequeaths a thousand dirhams on condition that he pay someone five hundred on his behalf: not permissible. If he says 'on condition that he pay so-and-so five hundred from them,' it is permissible. Al-‘Ala in the Nawadir of Hisham from Abu Yusuf: If he says 'when I die and these two slaves are in my possession, they are a bequest for so-and-so' and one slave dies, then the testator dies and the second is in his possession: the bequest is void. If he says 'when I die and so-and-so and so-and-so are alive, this slave is a bequest for them' and one of them dies before the testator's death: the other of them takes half the slave. He said: If a man bequeaths that his female slave be freed on condition that she marry, then the testator dies, and the slave girl says 'I will not marry,' she is freed. And it must be known that when the testator attaches the freeing of his slave to something after his death, it is either of two ways: He attaches it to a non-time-bound action, like 'she is free if she remains Muslim after my death' or 'he bequeaths that they free her after his death on condition that she does not marry' or 'she is free after my death if she does not marry.' Or he attaches her freeing to a time-bound action, like 'if she stays with my child for a month, she is free' or 'if she is sold and she says [incomplete]'
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles numerous transmitted rulings (nawadir) on conditional bequests, acceptance, rejection, and related issues. Key points include: (1) A bequest conditioned on performing Hajj is valid if accepted. (2) If a legatee is absent at the testator's death, it is treated as rejection unless he later accepts and gets the past benefit. (3) Scenarios where a bequest is made to an alternative if the first refuses; rulings depend on whether the first dies before or after the testator, and whether he had knowledge. (4) Bequests of service followed by freedom: the slave serves the heirs first if the legatee refuses? (5) Bequest to a wife/mother (umm walad) conditioned on caring for children; if she marries or leaves, it is cancelled. (6) Bequest conditioned on performing Hajj or jihad: the recipient owns the property and may use it freely. (7) Bequest with condition to pay a debt: validity depends on whether debt and one-third are known, and whether the one-third contains cash; if dirhams exceed debt, it is invalid due to riba. (8) Bequest of slaves conditional on survival: if one slave dies before testator, the bequest fails. (9) Bequest to free a slave conditioned on marriage: if the slave refuses marriage, she is freed. The passage ends with a classification of conditional freeing (ta'liq al-‘itq) after death: non-time-bound vs. time-bound.

Key Terms
غزوا (ghazw): A military expedition for jihad; in this context, a condition to perform jihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a testator says 'this house is for you on condition that you perform Hajj,' what can the legatee do with the house?
A) Only use it for Hajj-related purposes
B) Must sell it and use proceeds for Hajj
C) Can use it as he wishes, including selling it
D) Cannot accept the bequest without performing Hajj first

Key Takeaway
Conditions of worship in a bequest do not restrict ownership; the legatee gains absolute title.

Bequest with Condition to Pay Debt: Riba Issues
Ruling on bequest conditioned on debt payment with riba analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the validity of a bequest conditioned on paying the testator's debt, applying Hanafi rules on knowledge and riba.

Core Idea
A bequest conditioned on paying a debt is void if the debt or the one-third is unknown, or if the one-third contains money exceeding the debt (riba), but valid if the money is less than the debt.

This lesson tackles a complex ruling from Abu Yusuf on bequests where the legatee must pay the testator's debt. The validity hinges on the clarity of the debt amount and the composition of the bequeathed one-third, especially if it contains dirhams (cash), due to potential riba (interest) in exchanging money for money with a surplus of other goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and conditions
The ruling states: if the debt or one-third is unknown, the bequest is void. If both are known, the validity depends on whether the one-third contains gold/silver and the amount relative to the debt.
Knowledge (ma'lum) is a key shart.
2
Analyze the riba condition
If the one-third includes dirhams equal/more than the debt, it becomes a suspicious transaction of dirhams for dirhams with extra goods, which is not permissible. If dirhams are less than the debt, it is permissible.
This is a strict application of riba al-fadl rules to bequests.
3
Apply the immediate payment exception
If the legatee takes possession at the hour of death and pays immediately, deductions can be made to avoid riba.
This shows a pragmatic out to preserve the bequest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي نوادر بشر عن أبي يوسف في الإملاء : إذا أوصى بثلثه لرجل على أن يحج عنه فهذا جائز إن قبل ذلك الموصى له ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف : إذا قال في وصيته ينفق على فلان كذا والموصى له غائب أو مات الموصي وهو غائب فهو بمنزلة رد الوصية ولا شيء له، وكذلك إن قدم فلم يقبل، وإن قدم وقبل فله ما مضى. قال أبو يوسف : أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وقال أن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له الأول أو لم يأب فالثلث للأول ولو أبي كان للآخر، لو قال ثلثي وصية لفلان فإن لم يشأ ذلك فلفلان فهو مثل الأول، ولو قال ثلثي وصية لفلان إن شاء وإن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له قبل أن يتكلم بشيء فالثلث مردود على الورثة. ابن سماعة عن محمد: رجل أوصى لرجل بوصية ولا لفلان فقال فلان لا هي وقال إن لم يقبل فلان ما أوصيت له به أو قال إن رد فلان ما أوصيت به فهو لفلان فإذا الموصى له الأول حياً أو كان حياً فمات قبل الموصي ولم يعلم بالوصية قال هي للثاني كلها إن أسلمت جاريتي هذه فأعتقوها فباعوها قبل أن تسلم ثم أسلمت بعد مضي البيع صح ترد. قال أبو حنيفة : إذا قال أوصيت أن يخدم عبدي فلاناً سنة ثم هو أقبل الوصية قال : يخدم الورثة سنة ثم الموصى له ولا تبطل وصيته للثاني بأباء الأول الخدمة. قال أعطوه فلاناً بعد السنة فإن مات فلان خدم تمام السنة للورثة ثم يدفع إلى الموصى له بعد تمام السنة. وقال أبو حنيفة هذه وصية فيها يمين وليست المسألة الأولى كهذه ابراهيم بن رستم عن محمد قال أرضي التي في موضع كذا وغلامي فلان لأم ولده فيصير ميراثاً منها . ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف : أوصى أن ينفق على أم ولده ما قامت على ولدها وقال إن تزوجت فلا شيء لها فتزوجت وطلقها زوجها فرجعت إلى ولدها لم يرد عليها ما كان أوصى به لها وقد بطل ذلك، وكذلك إن خرجت من بلادها إلى بلاد أخرى، ولو خرجت من دارها أو جاء منها شيء يعرف أنها قد تركتهم ولم تقم عليهم فلا هذه الدار لك على أن تحج في سبيل الله أو قال هذه الدابة لك على أن تغزوا عليها في سبيل الله قال : له وله أن يصنع بها ما شاء. عن أبي يوسف : رجل أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وشرط عليه أن يقضي دينه معناه شرط الموصي على الموصى له أن يقضي دين الموصي فهذا على وجوه : إن كان الدين مجهولاً أو كان معلوماً إلا أن الثلث مجهول فالوصية باطلة وإن كان الدين معلوماً والثلث معلوماً فإن لم يكن في الثلث ذهب ولا فضة فهو جائز ويجب له الثلث بالدين إذا قبل كما يجب في البيع، وإن كان في الثلث دراهم إن كان أكثر من الدين فإن هذا لا يجوز من قبيل أن هذا دراهم بدراهم وفضل عروض سوى ذلك، وإن كانت الدراهم التي في الثلث أقل من الدين جاز، فإن قبض الثلث ساعة يموت أو قبض الدراهم التي في الثلث ساعة يموت وقضى الدين ساعته انتقص ذلك في الدراهم ما يخصه وجاز في العروض. أوصى بألف درهم على أن يقضي عنه فلاناً خمسمائة لا يجوز ولو قال على أن يقضي فلاناً منها خمسمائة جاز العلاء في نوادر هشام عن أبي يوسف : إذا قال إذا مت وهذان العبدان في ملكي فهما وصية لفلان فمات أحد العبدين ثم مات الموصي والثاني في ملكه فالوصية باطلة ولو قال إن مت وفلان وفلان حيان فهذا العبد وصية لهما فمات أحدهما قبل موت الموصي فإن الثاني منهما يعطي نصف العبد . قال : وإذا أوصى رجل لأمته أن تعتق على أن تتزوج ثم مات الموصي الأمة لا أتزوج فإنها تعتق ويجب أن يعلم بأن الموصي متى علق عتق مملوكه بشيء بعد موته فإنه لا يخلو من وجهين : أن يعلقه على فعل غير مؤقت بأن قال هي حرة إن ثبتت على الإسلام بعد موتي أو أوصى أن يعتقوها بعد موته على أن لا تتزوج أو قال هي حرة بعد موتي إن لم تتزوج أو علق عتقه على فعل مؤقت بأن قال إن مكثت مع ولدي شهراً فهي حرة أو بيع فقالت
And in the Nawadir of Bishr from Abu Yusuf in al-Imla': If he bequeaths one-third to a man on condition that he perform Hajj on his behalf, it is permissible if the legatee accepts. Ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf: If he says in his bequest 'spend such-and-such on so-and-so' and the legatee is absent, or the testator dies while he is absent, it is equivalent to rejection of the bequest and he gets nothing. Similarly if he comes and does not accept. But if he comes and accepts, he gets what has passed. Abu Yusuf said: He bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and says 'if he refuses, it is for so-and-so.' Then the first legatee dies or does not refuse: one-third is for the first; if he refuses, it is for the other. If he says 'one-third is a bequest for so-and-so; if he does not wish it, then for so-and-so,' it is like the first. If he says 'one-third is a bequest for so-and-so; if he wishes, and if he refuses, then for so-and-so,' and the legatee dies before saying anything, the one-third reverts to the heirs. Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad: A man bequeaths a bequest to a man and to so-and-so, and so-and-so says 'no, it is [for the other]'. And if he says 'if so-and-so does not accept my bequest to him' or 'if so-and-so rejects my bequest, then it is for so-and-so,' then if the first legatee is alive or was alive and died before the testator unaware of the bequest, he said: it is all for the second. 'If my slave-girl becomes Muslim, free her.' They sold her before she became Muslim, then she became Muslim after the sale had passed; the sale is valid (tard?). Abu Hanifa said: If he says 'I bequeath that my slave serve so-and-so for a year, then he is free,' and the legatee accepts the bequest, he said: the slave serves the heirs for a year, then the legatee, and his bequest to the second is not invalidated by the first's refusal of service. He said: Give him to so-and-so after the year. If so-and-so dies, the slave completes the year for the heirs, then is given to the legatee after the year. And Abu Hanifa said: This bequest contains an oath; the first issue is not like this. Ibrahim ibn Rustam from Muhammad said: 'My land in such place and my slave so-and-so are for my umm walad' – it becomes inheritance from her. Ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf: He bequeaths that maintenance be given to his umm walad as long as she cares for his children, and says 'if she marries, nothing for her.' She marries, but her husband divorces her and she returns to his children: he never returns to her what was bequeathed; it is cancelled. Similarly if she leaves her country to another country. Even if she leaves her house, or something comes from her indicating she has abandoned them and does not care for them, [it is cancelled]. 'This house is for you on condition that you perform Hajj in the way of Allah,' or he said 'this animal is for you on condition that you perform ghazw with it in the way of Allah,' he said: it is for him, and he may do with it as he wishes. From Abu Yusuf: A man bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and stipulates that he pay his debt. The meaning is that the testator stipulates on the legatee to pay the testator's debt. This has aspects: If the debt is unknown, or known but the one-third is unknown, the bequest is void. If the debt is known and the one-third is known, and the one-third contains no gold or silver, it is permissible, and he is obligated to [pay] the one-third for the debt if he accepts, as in a sale. If there are dirhams in the one-third and it is more than the debt, it is not permissible because it is dirhams for dirhams with an excess of goods besides. If the dirhams in the one-third are less than the debt, it is permissible. If he takes possession of the one-third at the hour of death, or takes the dirhams in the one-third at the hour of death and pays the debt immediately, he deducts from the dirhams what is appropriate, and it is permissible for the goods. He bequeaths a thousand dirhams on condition that he pay someone five hundred on his behalf: not permissible. If he says 'on condition that he pay so-and-so five hundred from them,' it is permissible. Al-‘Ala in the Nawadir of Hisham from Abu Yusuf: If he says 'when I die and these two slaves are in my possession, they are a bequest for so-and-so' and one slave dies, then the testator dies and the second is in his possession: the bequest is void. If he says 'when I die and so-and-so and so-and-so are alive, this slave is a bequest for them' and one of them dies before the testator's death: the other of them takes half the slave. He said: If a man bequeaths that his female slave be freed on condition that she marry, then the testator dies, and the slave girl says 'I will not marry,' she is freed. And it must be known that when the testator attaches the freeing of his slave to something after his death, it is either of two ways: He attaches it to a non-time-bound action, like 'she is free if she remains Muslim after my death' or 'he bequeaths that they free her after his death on condition that she does not marry' or 'she is free after my death if she does not marry.' Or he attaches her freeing to a time-bound action, like 'if she stays with my child for a month, she is free' or 'if she is sold and she says [incomplete]'

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles numerous transmitted rulings (nawadir) on conditional bequests, acceptance, rejection, and related issues. Key points include: (1) A bequest conditioned on performing Hajj is valid if accepted. (2) If a legatee is absent at the testator's death, it is treated as rejection unless he later accepts and gets the past benefit. (3) Scenarios where a bequest is made to an alternative if the first refuses; rulings depend on whether the first dies before or after the testator, and whether he had knowledge. (4) Bequests of service followed by freedom: the slave serves the heirs first if the legatee refuses? (5) Bequest to a wife/mother (umm walad) conditioned on caring for children; if she marries or leaves, it is cancelled. (6) Bequest conditioned on performing Hajj or jihad: the recipient owns the property and may use it freely. (7) Bequest with condition to pay a debt: validity depends on whether debt and one-third are known, and whether the one-third contains cash; if dirhams exceed debt, it is invalid due to riba. (8) Bequest of slaves conditional on survival: if one slave dies before testator, the bequest fails. (9) Bequest to free a slave conditioned on marriage: if the slave refuses marriage, she is freed. The passage ends with a classification of conditional freeing (ta'liq al-‘itq) after death: non-time-bound vs. time-bound.

Key Terms
ربا (riba): Unlawful increase or interest; in this context, the forbidden excess in exchanging monetary items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, why is a bequest of 1000 dirhams on condition that the legatee pay 500 dirhams to someone else invalid?
A) The condition is not accepted
B) The debt is unknown
C) It resembles a sale of dirhams for dirhams with uncertainty (gharar)
D) The amount is not permissible because it's a condition without specifying 'from them'

Key Takeaway
A bequest conditioned on paying a debt is scrutinized for riba; it is valid only when the cash portion of the bequest does not exceed the debt or is handled with immediate payment.

Conditional Freeing of Slaves and Bequests of Slaves
Rulings on conditional bequests of slaves and conditional freeing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on bequests of slaves conditional on survival and conditional freeing after death, distinguishing between time-bound and non-time-bound conditions.

Core Idea
A bequest of slaves conditional on their survival at the testator's death fails if one dies earlier; conditional freeing after death depends on the nature of the condition being time-bound or not.

This lesson examines two related issues: bequests of slaves where the testator conditions the bequest on the slaves being alive at his death, and bequests involving the freeing of a slave after death with conditions. The rulings from Hisham and Abu Yusuf clarify the outcomes when the condition is not fully met.

Guided Path
1
Bequest of slaves conditional on survival
If the testator says 'these two slaves are a bequest for X if they are in my possession at my death' and one dies before him, the bequest is void for both.
The condition is conjunctive.
2
Bequest of a slave to two people conditional on survival
If the testator says 'this slave is a bequest for A and B if they are alive at my death' and one dies, the other takes half the slave.
The condition applies per legatee; the surviving legatee takes his share.
3
Conditional freeing (ta'liq al-'itq) after death
The testator may condition freeing on a non-time-bound action (e.g., remaining Muslim) or a time-bound action (staying for a month). If the slave refuses a condition (e.g., not marrying), she is freed anyway because the condition is not binding.
The classification helps determine enforceability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي نوادر بشر عن أبي يوسف في الإملاء : إذا أوصى بثلثه لرجل على أن يحج عنه فهذا جائز إن قبل ذلك الموصى له ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف : إذا قال في وصيته ينفق على فلان كذا والموصى له غائب أو مات الموصي وهو غائب فهو بمنزلة رد الوصية ولا شيء له، وكذلك إن قدم فلم يقبل، وإن قدم وقبل فله ما مضى. قال أبو يوسف : أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وقال أن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له الأول أو لم يأب فالثلث للأول ولو أبي كان للآخر، لو قال ثلثي وصية لفلان فإن لم يشأ ذلك فلفلان فهو مثل الأول، ولو قال ثلثي وصية لفلان إن شاء وإن أبى فهو لفلان فمات الموصى له قبل أن يتكلم بشيء فالثلث مردود على الورثة. ابن سماعة عن محمد: رجل أوصى لرجل بوصية ولا لفلان فقال فلان لا هي وقال إن لم يقبل فلان ما أوصيت له به أو قال إن رد فلان ما أوصيت به فهو لفلان فإذا الموصى له الأول حياً أو كان حياً فمات قبل الموصي ولم يعلم بالوصية قال هي للثاني كلها إن أسلمت جاريتي هذه فأعتقوها فباعوها قبل أن تسلم ثم أسلمت بعد مضي البيع صح ترد. قال أبو حنيفة : إذا قال أوصيت أن يخدم عبدي فلاناً سنة ثم هو أقبل الوصية قال : يخدم الورثة سنة ثم الموصى له ولا تبطل وصيته للثاني بأباء الأول الخدمة. قال أعطوه فلاناً بعد السنة فإن مات فلان خدم تمام السنة للورثة ثم يدفع إلى الموصى له بعد تمام السنة. وقال أبو حنيفة هذه وصية فيها يمين وليست المسألة الأولى كهذه ابراهيم بن رستم عن محمد قال أرضي التي في موضع كذا وغلامي فلان لأم ولده فيصير ميراثاً منها . ابن سماعة عن أبي يوسف : أوصى أن ينفق على أم ولده ما قامت على ولدها وقال إن تزوجت فلا شيء لها فتزوجت وطلقها زوجها فرجعت إلى ولدها لم يرد عليها ما كان أوصى به لها وقد بطل ذلك، وكذلك إن خرجت من بلادها إلى بلاد أخرى، ولو خرجت من دارها أو جاء منها شيء يعرف أنها قد تركتهم ولم تقم عليهم فلا هذه الدار لك على أن تحج في سبيل الله أو قال هذه الدابة لك على أن تغزوا عليها في سبيل الله قال : له وله أن يصنع بها ما شاء. عن أبي يوسف : رجل أوصى بثلث ماله لرجل وشرط عليه أن يقضي دينه معناه شرط الموصي على الموصى له أن يقضي دين الموصي فهذا على وجوه : إن كان الدين مجهولاً أو كان معلوماً إلا أن الثلث مجهول فالوصية باطلة وإن كان الدين معلوماً والثلث معلوماً فإن لم يكن في الثلث ذهب ولا فضة فهو جائز ويجب له الثلث بالدين إذا قبل كما يجب في البيع، وإن كان في الثلث دراهم إن كان أكثر من الدين فإن هذا لا يجوز من قبيل أن هذا دراهم بدراهم وفضل عروض سوى ذلك، وإن كانت الدراهم التي في الثلث أقل من الدين جاز، فإن قبض الثلث ساعة يموت أو قبض الدراهم التي في الثلث ساعة يموت وقضى الدين ساعته انتقص ذلك في الدراهم ما يخصه وجاز في العروض. أوصى بألف درهم على أن يقضي عنه فلاناً خمسمائة لا يجوز ولو قال على أن يقضي فلاناً منها خمسمائة جاز العلاء في نوادر هشام عن أبي يوسف : إذا قال إذا مت وهذان العبدان في ملكي فهما وصية لفلان فمات أحد العبدين ثم مات الموصي والثاني في ملكه فالوصية باطلة ولو قال إن مت وفلان وفلان حيان فهذا العبد وصية لهما فمات أحدهما قبل موت الموصي فإن الثاني منهما يعطي نصف العبد . قال : وإذا أوصى رجل لأمته أن تعتق على أن تتزوج ثم مات الموصي الأمة لا أتزوج فإنها تعتق ويجب أن يعلم بأن الموصي متى علق عتق مملوكه بشيء بعد موته فإنه لا يخلو من وجهين : أن يعلقه على فعل غير مؤقت بأن قال هي حرة إن ثبتت على الإسلام بعد موتي أو أوصى أن يعتقوها بعد موته على أن لا تتزوج أو قال هي حرة بعد موتي إن لم تتزوج أو علق عتقه على فعل مؤقت بأن قال إن مكثت مع ولدي شهراً فهي حرة أو بيع فقالت
And in the Nawadir of Bishr from Abu Yusuf in al-Imla': If he bequeaths one-third to a man on condition that he perform Hajj on his behalf, it is permissible if the legatee accepts. Ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf: If he says in his bequest 'spend such-and-such on so-and-so' and the legatee is absent, or the testator dies while he is absent, it is equivalent to rejection of the bequest and he gets nothing. Similarly if he comes and does not accept. But if he comes and accepts, he gets what has passed. Abu Yusuf said: He bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and says 'if he refuses, it is for so-and-so.' Then the first legatee dies or does not refuse: one-third is for the first; if he refuses, it is for the other. If he says 'one-third is a bequest for so-and-so; if he does not wish it, then for so-and-so,' it is like the first. If he says 'one-third is a bequest for so-and-so; if he wishes, and if he refuses, then for so-and-so,' and the legatee dies before saying anything, the one-third reverts to the heirs. Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad: A man bequeaths a bequest to a man and to so-and-so, and so-and-so says 'no, it is [for the other]'. And if he says 'if so-and-so does not accept my bequest to him' or 'if so-and-so rejects my bequest, then it is for so-and-so,' then if the first legatee is alive or was alive and died before the testator unaware of the bequest, he said: it is all for the second. 'If my slave-girl becomes Muslim, free her.' They sold her before she became Muslim, then she became Muslim after the sale had passed; the sale is valid (tard?). Abu Hanifa said: If he says 'I bequeath that my slave serve so-and-so for a year, then he is free,' and the legatee accepts the bequest, he said: the slave serves the heirs for a year, then the legatee, and his bequest to the second is not invalidated by the first's refusal of service. He said: Give him to so-and-so after the year. If so-and-so dies, the slave completes the year for the heirs, then is given to the legatee after the year. And Abu Hanifa said: This bequest contains an oath; the first issue is not like this. Ibrahim ibn Rustam from Muhammad said: 'My land in such place and my slave so-and-so are for my umm walad' – it becomes inheritance from her. Ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf: He bequeaths that maintenance be given to his umm walad as long as she cares for his children, and says 'if she marries, nothing for her.' She marries, but her husband divorces her and she returns to his children: he never returns to her what was bequeathed; it is cancelled. Similarly if she leaves her country to another country. Even if she leaves her house, or something comes from her indicating she has abandoned them and does not care for them, [it is cancelled]. 'This house is for you on condition that you perform Hajj in the way of Allah,' or he said 'this animal is for you on condition that you perform ghazw with it in the way of Allah,' he said: it is for him, and he may do with it as he wishes. From Abu Yusuf: A man bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and stipulates that he pay his debt. The meaning is that the testator stipulates on the legatee to pay the testator's debt. This has aspects: If the debt is unknown, or known but the one-third is unknown, the bequest is void. If the debt is known and the one-third is known, and the one-third contains no gold or silver, it is permissible, and he is obligated to [pay] the one-third for the debt if he accepts, as in a sale. If there are dirhams in the one-third and it is more than the debt, it is not permissible because it is dirhams for dirhams with an excess of goods besides. If the dirhams in the one-third are less than the debt, it is permissible. If he takes possession of the one-third at the hour of death, or takes the dirhams in the one-third at the hour of death and pays the debt immediately, he deducts from the dirhams what is appropriate, and it is permissible for the goods. He bequeaths a thousand dirhams on condition that he pay someone five hundred on his behalf: not permissible. If he says 'on condition that he pay so-and-so five hundred from them,' it is permissible. Al-‘Ala in the Nawadir of Hisham from Abu Yusuf: If he says 'when I die and these two slaves are in my possession, they are a bequest for so-and-so' and one slave dies, then the testator dies and the second is in his possession: the bequest is void. If he says 'when I die and so-and-so and so-and-so are alive, this slave is a bequest for them' and one of them dies before the testator's death: the other of them takes half the slave. He said: If a man bequeaths that his female slave be freed on condition that she marry, then the testator dies, and the slave girl says 'I will not marry,' she is freed. And it must be known that when the testator attaches the freeing of his slave to something after his death, it is either of two ways: He attaches it to a non-time-bound action, like 'she is free if she remains Muslim after my death' or 'he bequeaths that they free her after his death on condition that she does not marry' or 'she is free after my death if she does not marry.' Or he attaches her freeing to a time-bound action, like 'if she stays with my child for a month, she is free' or 'if she is sold and she says [incomplete]'
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles numerous transmitted rulings (nawadir) on conditional bequests, acceptance, rejection, and related issues. Key points include: (1) A bequest conditioned on performing Hajj is valid if accepted. (2) If a legatee is absent at the testator's death, it is treated as rejection unless he later accepts and gets the past benefit. (3) Scenarios where a bequest is made to an alternative if the first refuses; rulings depend on whether the first dies before or after the testator, and whether he had knowledge. (4) Bequests of service followed by freedom: the slave serves the heirs first if the legatee refuses? (5) Bequest to a wife/mother (umm walad) conditioned on caring for children; if she marries or leaves, it is cancelled. (6) Bequest conditioned on performing Hajj or jihad: the recipient owns the property and may use it freely. (7) Bequest with condition to pay a debt: validity depends on whether debt and one-third are known, and whether the one-third contains cash; if dirhams exceed debt, it is invalid due to riba. (8) Bequest of slaves conditional on survival: if one slave dies before testator, the bequest fails. (9) Bequest to free a slave conditioned on marriage: if the slave refuses marriage, she is freed. The passage ends with a classification of conditional freeing (ta'liq al-‘itq) after death: non-time-bound vs. time-bound.

Key Terms
تعليق العتق (ta'liq al-'itq): The conditional freeing of a slave, suspended upon a future event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a testator says 'my slave is free after my death if she stays with my child for one month,' and the slave does not stay, what happens?
A) She is freed anyway
B) She is not freed
C) She is freed but must compensate
D) The bequest is void

Key Takeaway
In conditional bequests of slaves, the exact conditions must be met; in conditional freeing, non-time-bound conditions are not enforceable, ensuring freedom.

Distinguishing Wills from Acknowledgments and Gifts by Wording
Explaining which verbal expressions constitute a valid will vs. acknowledgment or gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the verbal expressions that constitute a will versus an acknowledgment or gift in Hanafi law, and apply the rule of istihsan where applicable.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the precise wording determines whether a declaration is a will, acknowledgment, or gift.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the subtle distinctions between testamentary dispositions and other declarations based on the exact phrasing used. Understanding these nuances is essential for drafting valid wills and avoiding unintended legal consequences. The passage also highlights the use of istiḥsān to override strict analogy in certain borderline cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the declaration type based on the particle
When 'awṣaytu' (I bequeathed) directly introduces a person and property, it is a will. When it is followed by the particle 'an' (that) and a clause, it becomes an acknowledgment because 'an' changes the meaning to 'I mentioned'.
Example: 'Awṣaytu li-fulān bi-alf' = will; 'Awṣaytu an li-fulān fī mālī alf' = acknowledgment.
2
Distinguish using 'min' vs 'fī' for property
In the context of a will, saying 'one-sixth of my house is for so-and-so' (using 'min') is a will. Saying 'for so-and-so one-sixth in my house' (using 'fī') is an acknowledgment because 'fī' indicates an existing right.
Prepositions matter: 'min' suggests allocation, 'fī' suggests ownership.
3
Apply istiḥsān when a gift is mentioned within a will
If a person says 'this slave is for so-and-so' without mentioning death or a will, it is a gift by both qiyās and istiḥsān. However, if mentioned during a will, qiyās would make it a will, but istiḥsān (the relied-upon view) keeps it as a gift requiring possession in life.
The preferred view is istiḥsān, as cited from al-Ṭawāwīsī.
4
Note the effect of 'after my death'
If the testator explicitly says 'after my death', the declaration becomes a will, even if it uses the word 'gift'. This is because a gift after death is essentially a will.
Such a will is valid even if the property is undivided (shuyūʻ) and possession is not required during the testator's lifetime.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان الألفاظ التي تكون وصية والتي لا تكون وصية روى ابن سماعة في نوادره عن محمد: إذا قال الرجل أشهدوا أني أوصيت لفلان بألف درهم وأوصيت بأن لفلان في مالي ألف درهم فالألف الأولى وصية والأخرى إقرار والفرق أن أوصيت لما دخلت على «أن» المصدرية تستعمل بمعنى ذكرت ولهذا كان إقراراً بخلاف الأولى فإنها على بابها . وفي الأصل : إذا قال في وصيته سدس داري لفلان وأني أجيز ذلك يكون وصية، ولو قال سدس في داري لفلان وإني أجيز ذلك يكون وصية، ولو قال لفلان سدس في داري فإنه يكون إقراراً، وعلى هذا إذا قال الرجل لفلان درهم من مالي يكون وصية استحساناً، وإن كان في ذكر وصيته إذا قال في مالي كان إقراراً، وإذا قال عبدي هذا لفلان وذاري هذه لفلان ولم يقل وصية ولا كان في ذكر وصيه ولا بعد موتي كانت هبة قياساً واستحساناً، وإن قبضها في حال حياته صح، وإن لم يقبضها حتى مات فهو باطل، وإن ذكرها في خلال الوصية ذكر الشيخ الإمام الزاهد أحمد الطواويسي في شرح وصايا الأصل القياس أن يكون هذا وصية، وفي الاستحسان لا يكون وصية. وإذا قال أوصيت أن يوهب لفلان سدس داري بعد موتي كان ذلك وصية عملاً بقوله بعد موتي فالهبة بعد الموت هي الوصية فتصح مع الشيوع ولا يشترط قبضه في حيات الموصي .
And as for the explanation of the words that constitute a will and those that do not constitute a will: Ibn Samāʻah narrated in his Nawādir from Muḥammad: When a man says 'Bear witness that I have bequeathed to so-and-so a thousand dirhams and I have bequeathed that so-and-so has a thousand dirhams in my wealth,' the first thousand is a will and the other is an acknowledgment. The difference is that 'I have bequeathed' when it enters on the subordinating 'an' is used in the sense of 'I mentioned,' and therefore it is an acknowledgment, unlike the first which is used in its proper sense. And in al-Aṣl: If he says in his will 'One-sixth of my house is for so-and-so and that I permit that,' it is a will. And if he says 'One-sixth in my house is for so-and-so and I permit that,' it is a will. And if he says 'For so-and-so one-sixth in my house,' it is an acknowledgment. And on this basis, if a man says 'For so-and-so a dirham from my wealth,' it is a will by istiḥsān, although if he says 'In my wealth' it is an acknowledgment. And if he says 'This my slave is for so-and-so and this my house is for so-and-so' and does not say 'will' nor is it in the context of his will nor after my death, it is a gift by qiyās and istiḥsān. If he takes possession in his lifetime, it is valid; if he does not take possession until he dies, it is void. And if he mentions it in the course of a will, Shaykh al-Imām al-Zāhid Aḥmad al-Ṭawāwīsī mentioned in the commentary on Waṣāyā al-Aṣl that by qiyās this would be a will, and by istiḥsān it is not a will. And if he says 'I have bequeathed that one-sixth of my house be given as a gift to so-and-so after my death,' that is a will, acting on his saying 'after my death,' so the gift after death is the will; thus it is valid despite the common ownership, and possession is not required during the testator's life.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a legal analysis of the expressions that constitute a valid will (waṣiyyah) as opposed to an acknowledgment (iqrār) or a gift (hibah) in Hanafi law. The core distinction is based on the wording and context. If a person uses the phrase 'I have bequeathed' (awṣaytu) directly to a person, it is a will. But if he says 'I have bequeathed that' (awṣaytu an) followed by a clause that states a debt or entitlement, it is considered an acknowledgment because 'an' turns it into a statement of fact rather than a testamentary disposition. The text from al-Aṣl (the corpus of Imam Muḥammad) provides further examples: saying 'one-sixth of my house is for so-and-so' in the context of a will is a will, while 'for so-and-so one-sixth in my house' is an acknowledgment because the preposition 'in' (fī) indicates an existing right. There is also a discussion of gifts: if someone says 'this slave is for so-and-so' without mentioning death or will, it is a gift, requiring delivery in the donor's lifetime. If mentioned within a will, there is a difference between qiyās (analogy) and istiḥsān (juristic preference). The ruling is that a gift after death (hibah baʻd al-mawt) is a will, valid even if the property is undivided (shuyūʻ), and no possession is required during the testator's life because the transfer occurs at death. This passage highlights the Hanafi attention to precise wording in determining the legal nature of a person's declaration.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment of an existing right or debt, as opposed to a testamentary disposition.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference used to override strict analogy (qiyas) for reasons of equity or practical convenience.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning; the strict ruling by analogy in this passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone says 'I have bequeathed that so-and-so has a thousand dirhams in my wealth', is it a will or an acknowledgment?
A) It is a will because he used the word 'bequeathed'.
B) It is an acknowledgment because 'an' changes the meaning to 'I mentioned'.
C) It is a gift because he mentioned 'in my wealth'.
D) It depends on whether he said 'after my death'.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the precise wording—especially the presence of 'an' or prepositions like 'fī'—determines whether a declaration is a will, acknowledgment, or gift, and istiḥsān may override strict analogy in borderline cases.
